        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2906292727" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4928987840139515473"><i>We filled up life with living,<br/>with grins, scabbed knees, and noise.<br/>In glass I see an older man,<br/>but this book's for the boys.</i><br/><br/><i>"In me are the memories of a boy's life, spent in that realm of enchantments."</i><br/><br/><b>What. A. Wonderful. Book.!!!</b><br/><br/>Boy's Life goes directly into my favorites shelf. This novel which is about a boy's life, is <b>special, magical, exceptional and feels so real</b>.<br/><br/>The narrator of this autobiographical fiction, Cory Mackenson, tells us: <br/><blockquote>"We all start out knowing magic. We are born with whirlw</blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText4928987840139515473" style="display:none"><i>We filled up life with living,<br />with grins, scabbed knees, and noise.<br />In glass I see an older man,<br />but this book's for the boys.</i><br /><br /><i>"In me are the memories of a boy's life, spent in that realm of enchantments."</i><br /><br /><b>What. A. Wonderful. Book.!!!</b><br /><br />Boy's Life goes directly into my favorites shelf. This novel which is about a boy's life, is <b>special, magical, exceptional and feels so real</b>.<br /><br />The narrator of this autobiographical fiction, Cory Mackenson, tells us: <br /><blockquote>"We all start out knowing magic. We are born with whirlwinds, forest fires, and comets inside us. We are born able to sing to birds and read the clouds and see our destiny in grains of sand. But then we get the magic educated right out of our souls. We get it churched out, spanked out, washed out, and combed out. We get put on the straight and narrow and told to be responsible. The truth of life is that every year we get farther away from the essence that is born within us."</blockquote><br />Don't read any further reviews, just pick up the book and read, it will be an enjoyable journey...</span>

<div id="review_1663695564" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1663695564" />
    <a title="Bill Khaemba" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/41380936-bill-khaemba"><img alt="Bill Khaemba" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1561102062p2/41380936.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1663695564?book_show_action=true">Jun 09, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bill Khaemba" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bill Khaemba" href="/user/show/41380936-bill-khaemba">Bill Khaemba</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41380936-bill-khaemba?shelf=fav-2016">fav-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41380936-bill-khaemba?shelf=favorite-books-fantastic-reads">favorite-books-fantastic-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41380936-bill-khaemba?shelf=highly-rated-books">highly-rated-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41380936-bill-khaemba?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41380936-bill-khaemba?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41380936-bill-khaemba?shelf=fantasy-epic-magic-adventure">fantasy-epic-magic-adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41380936-bill-khaemba?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41380936-bill-khaemba?shelf=classic">classic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41380936-bill-khaemba?shelf=magical-realism">magical-realism</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1663695564" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8625037829101153932"><b>
  "No!!! Why did it end…I don’t want to close the book, I don’t want to leave Zephyr, Alabama." (<del>Throws tantrum</del>)
</b><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1474658029ra/20629443.gif' width='320' height='176' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>This was truly magical absolutely breathtaking & one of the best books I have ever read… So much life came out of this book, the author (<em>
  <strong>bless him</strong>
</em>) managed to <b>
  
    <em>capture the true essence of childhood, the beauty of imagination and the importance of naivety</em>
  
</b>. The way most people describe the love for this book and the countless recommendation for this one, I can finally sa</span>
  <span id="freeText8625037829101153932" style="display:none"><b>
  "No!!! Why did it end…I don’t want to close the book, I don’t want to leave Zephyr, Alabama." (<del>Throws tantrum</del>)
</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1474658029ra/20629443.gif" width="320" height="176" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This was truly magical absolutely breathtaking &amp; one of the best books I have ever read… So much life came out of this book, the author (<em>
  <strong>bless him</strong>
</em>) managed to <b>
  
    <em>capture the true essence of childhood, the beauty of imagination and the importance of naivety</em>
  
</b>. The way most people describe the love for this book and the countless recommendation for this one, I can finally say I understand!!!! This is not only a book with pages but actual magic, the minute I closed the book after finishing I yearned for my childhood… From playing hide &amp; seek to wake up early Saturday to catch up on my cartoons and to remember the time I still believed magic actually exist <em>sigh</em><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1474658284ra/20629461.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Cory (<strong>
  <em>The main narrator</em>
</strong>) is a young lad living in <strong>Zephyr, Alabama</strong> in the 1960s, the small town is quite strange in a way. We see the beauty of being a child through his eyes and also the value of holding on to that inner innocence even as one grows up. <em>One day as he accompanies his father in one of his milk deliveries an accident occurs that will take him into one interesting adventure with lots of unusual characters along the way.</em><br><br>Honorable mention on one of the amazing passages…<br><b>
  <blockquote>
    <em>
      “See, this is my opinion: we all start out knowing magic. We are born with whirlwinds, forest fires, and comets inside us. We are born able to sing to birds and read the clouds and see our destiny in grains of sand. But then we get the magic educated right out of our souls. We get it churched out, spanked out, washed out, and combed out. We get put on the straight and narrow and told to be responsible. Told to act our age. Told to grow up, for God's sake. And you know why we were told that? Because the people doing the telling were afraid of our wildness and youth, and because the magic we knew made them ashamed and sad of what they'd allowed to wither in themselves.”
    </em>
  </blockquote>
</b><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1474658029ra/20629445.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I would honestly go into the book blind because you will watch the story unravel in a unique way, I will say that I expected more of a fantasy story but towards the end of the story I came to the realisation that the book in itself is magic. The way the character approached topics of death, love, religion, racism and other topics from his perspective was refreshing because he still kept asking certain questions a normal child would ask like<b> <em>“Why are black people and white people so distant if they all die and go to the same heaven?” or “Is faith real?” I found myself kind of relating to him on a whole other level. </em></b>The way Robert presents the story through the eyes of a 12-year-old child who is filled with imagination and an eye for the unusual added weight to the story. He painted such vivid images with his description of certain scenes and each character drowned out even though the story was told by a 12-year-old. I normally don’t get child narrators in stories, they usually come off too naïve or too pretentious but on this occasion, it was executed flawlessly.<br><b>
  <blockquote>
    <em>“No one ever grows up. They may look grown-up, but it's just the clay of time. Men and women are still children deep in their hearts." </em>Mrs<em> Neville”</em>
  </blockquote>
</b><br><br>I loved the writing style, it was so elegant with beautiful prose and so many moving quotes that broke me <del>(I cried so freaking hard man</del>) and discussions on<em>
   life after death, faith in religion, Racism in such a crucial time period, the simplicity of childhood
</em> etc. This book has completely altered my perspective on how I viewed the world … When I was a kid I always found solace in the little things like food, cartoons, road trips, Christmas mornings and so much. As I grew up society and adulthood came and fucked it up… expectations, adulthood, responsibility and all that evil stuff came to play but I always protected my inner childhood from that invasion. If I see a bouncing castle I would bloody jump on that shit, that first lick of a cold ice cream after a hot day is magic, Saturday cartoons are still my jam because If I don’t have those little things I would probably be in a mental institution.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1474658368ra/20629479.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>So if you want a book that will make you crave your childhood while altering your perspective as an adult pick this one up .<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1474658029ra/20629446.gif" alt="Image result for highly recommended gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>P.S. The only flaw with the book is i need a beautiful edition :)<br><b> This Edition </b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1456218682i/18203660._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><br><b> I just got this &amp; I can't wait </b> Literally everyone loves this!!!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1456234391ra/18207041.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="8625037829101153932" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2238186846" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2238186846" />
    <a title="Heidi The Reader" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7986781-heidi-the-reader"><img alt="Heidi The Reader" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593309467p2/7986781.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2238186846?book_show_action=true">Jan 12, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Heidi The Reader" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Heidi The Reader" href="/user/show/7986781-heidi-the-reader">Heidi The Reader</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7986781-heidi-the-reader?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7986781-heidi-the-reader?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2238186846" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17644228391603855839"><i> Boy's Life</i> is about Cory Mackenson, the southern town of Zephyr and the magic of every day life.<br/><br/><i>We had a monster in the river, and a secret in the lake. We had a ghost that haunted the road behind the wheel of a black dragster with flames on the hood. We had a Gabriel and a Lucifer, and a rebel that rose from the dead. We had an alien invader, a boy with a perfect arm, and we had a dinosaur loose on Merchants Street. It was a magic place."</i> pg 10, ebook.<br/><br/>The story begins with a death and a myster</span>
  <span id="freeText17644228391603855839" style="display:none"><i> Boy's Life</i> is about Cory Mackenson, the southern town of Zephyr and the magic of every day life.<br /><br /><i>We had a monster in the river, and a secret in the lake. We had a ghost that haunted the road behind the wheel of a black dragster with flames on the hood. We had a Gabriel and a Lucifer, and a rebel that rose from the dead. We had an alien invader, a boy with a perfect arm, and we had a dinosaur loose on Merchants Street. It was a magic place."</i> pg 10, ebook.<br /><br />The story begins with a death and a mystery. <i>"On that morning before the sun, as I sat eating my breakfast with my dad and mom in our house on Hilltop Street, the year was 1964. There were great changes in the winds of earth, things of which I was unaware."</i> pg 15.<br /><br />After witnessing something terrible sinking into the lake, Cory sets about discovering what or who put it there.<br /><br />The trauma is almost too much for Cory's father to bear. <i>"Whoever did it had to be a local. Had to be. ... It might be somebody who sits on our pew at church. Somebody we buy groceries or clothes from. Somebody we've known all our lives... or thought we knew. That scares me like I've never been scared before."</i> pg 35, ebook.<br /><br />But this book is about more than just the central mystery. It is also about the community of Zephyr and the relationships between the people who live there.<br /><br />There is a racial divide in the town. When the river overflows its banks, the white and black communities come together to prevent disaster. <i>"There is something about nature out of control that touches a primal terror. We are used to believing that we're the masters of our domain, and that God has given us this earth to rule over. ... The truth is more fearsome: we are as frail as young trees in tornadoes, and our beloved homes are one flood away from driftwood."</i> pg 97, ebook.<br /><br /><i>Boy's Life</i> also examines coming-of-age issues like bullies, over-bearing parents, and accepting the realities of old age and death. <i>"But I'll tell you a secret, Cory. Want to hear it?" I nodded. "No one," Mrs. Neville whispered, "ever grows up. ... They may look grown-up but it's a disguise. It's just the clay of time. Men and women are still children deep in their hearts."</i> pg 221, ebook.<br /><br />I loved this book. It is a far-reaching tale made for winter nights, to be read with a hot drink in your hand and a warm blanket on your lap.<br /><br />It vaguely reminded me of <i>The Help</i> because of its southern location, the racial issues and some of the mystery elements. But really, <i>Boy's Life</i> stands on its own.<br /><br />Recommended for readers who enjoy historical fiction with a touch of magic and mystery.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17644228391603855839" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2446508-agnieszka?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2446508-agnieszka?shelf=2017">2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2446508-agnieszka?shelf=fantasy-and-sf">fantasy-and-sf</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1904642221" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7526736581551765158"><br/><i> Boy’s life </i> is like colorful, multilayered crazy patchwork woven from boyish dreams and desires, a dash of magic and forgotten long time ago by our adult self power to fly. It’s a dish compounded from carefully chosen ingredients that tastes of sweetness of children’s smiles and bitterness of their tears. It’s entering to our dreamed secret garden, realm inhabited both by bloodthirsty monsters and noble sheriffs, heroes that occupied our childish imagination. It’s a nostalgic journey into the p</span>
  <span id="freeText7526736581551765158" style="display:none"><br /><i> Boy’s life </i> is like colorful, multilayered crazy patchwork woven from boyish dreams and desires, a dash of magic and forgotten long time ago by our adult self power to fly. It’s a dish compounded from carefully chosen ingredients that tastes of sweetness of children’s smiles and bitterness of their tears. It’s entering to our dreamed secret garden, realm inhabited both by bloodthirsty monsters and noble sheriffs, heroes that occupied our childish imagination. It’s a nostalgic journey into the past to pre-telly, computer and cell phone era, to the times when we really talked to each other, making stories and let our imagination run wild.<br /><br /><i> Boy’s life </i> is a foray to place where we lost some illusions and innocence gaining in return awareness that life doesn’t remind a comic book at all, that even children may be injured or die in accidents and that our four-footed friends are not allowed to enter with us in adulthood. But who said everybody gets happy ending ? It’s a brutal lesson of life, clash with the world of stronger and bullies, unjust law and racial prejudices and knowledge that our neighbours now and then like to dress up with ridiculous white robes ( the whole thing spans a year on the cusp of 1963/1964 in some jerkwater town called Zephyr, Alabama ).<br /><br />Cory, sensitive and imaginative teenager is a wonderful narrator of the story and perfect guide to that world. He opens generously doors to the distant land of childhood to let us for some precious moments get rid of stiff corset of adulthood and responsibility, to see things that we crave to do but it wouldn’t be appropriate for us to do them anymore, and taking our hand smoothly brings us through that lost kingdom. In his person reader can embrace own younger self and immerse in these magic childlike years, different in details but as a wholeness perfectly apt.<br /><br />And the message that we can't let slip magic away from our life, in whole it naivety, is something I'll gladly carry for the days to come. I found <i>Boy’s life </i> deprived of unnecessary didacticism or superfluous moralizing, the truth is that one can't protect kids from every evil of the world and what we really can is to listen to them, to what they are telling us and what's even more important what they're not telling. One can't wrap them in cotton wool, we have to let them learn from theirs own mistakes, gain cuts and bruises, sense of failure and broken hearts. But we may guard them and guide, lead them through life and one day just let them go to fly into the big wide world. And whether we send them into the world not breaking their wings is up to us.<br /><br />4.5/5</span>
  <a data-text-id="7526736581551765158" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_101825148" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/101825148" />
    <a title="Lou" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3699303-lou"><img alt="Lou" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1312212794p2/3699303.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/101825148?book_show_action=true">May 08, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lou" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lou" href="/user/show/3699303-lou">Lou</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3699303-lou?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3699303-lou?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3699303-lou?shelf=re-read-list">re-read-list</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3699303-lou?shelf=best-reads">best-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer101825148" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4692710637267333285">This is a Magical story of a boy Cory, he narrates to us about his life in the year 1964 in a small town of Zephyr Alabama where anything and everything happens. His experiences and friendships want to make you tearful and joyful he is on a journey of self discovery and of mysteries that haunt his father and the lake. A highly recommended read one to make my list of must reads, Robert McCammon is a underrated writer a master craftsman storyteller. <b>
  <blockquote>'Because Death cannot be known. It cannot be </blockquote></b></span>
  <span id="freeText4692710637267333285" style="display:none">This is a Magical story of a boy Cory, he narrates to us about his life in the year 1964 in a small town of Zephyr Alabama where anything and everything happens. His experiences and friendships want to make you tearful and joyful he is on a journey of self discovery and of mysteries that haunt his father and the lake. A highly recommended read one to make my list of must reads, Robert McCammon is a underrated writer a master craftsman storyteller. <b>
  <blockquote>'Because Death cannot be known. It cannot be befriended. If death were a boy, he would be a lonely figure, standing at the playground's edge while the air rippled with other children's laughter. If death were a boy, he would walk alone. He would speak in a whisper and his eyes would be haunted by knowledge no human can bear. This is what tore at me in the quiet hours: We came from darkness, and to darkness we must return.'</blockquote>
</b><br /><br />In a re-read,(May 2012) this time round I felt i discovered more in this wonderful<br /> Story.<br /> The dead, The Lake, the Dog, the bicycle and the girl in the water are maybe parts that I remember well and loved to revisit. <br /> There was also many things that I had forgotten and reliving it made it a joyful experience. It never tires to read those wonderful sentences that he puts together in this story.<br />When an author writes a story of youth and coming of age they sometimes included their own experiences.<br />In this novel we do see in parts a little peak into the writer Robert McCammon, for instance Golden apples of the Sun by Ray Brabury is mentioned in here as one of Cory's cherished reads and Robert McCammon has mentioned it as a book that he holds dear and recommends. <br />There are other things I have picked up on and they add to just how much a respected and talented writer he is.<br />This story hold a high place in my shelf in line with<br />To kill a mockingbird, <br />The Bottoms by Joe Lansdale, <br />Something wicked this way comes by Ray Bradbury <br />and Stand by Me by Stephen King.<br /><br />As Robert McCammon says in the final pages of this novel, in the acknowledgments, I too bid you farewell in his words...<br />Your lake will always be deeper and sweeter than mine, your jar hold greater mysteries, your rockets travel truer to the heart.<br /><br />These excerpts below are ones that I felt echoed a thousand heart felt feelings.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>"In later years I would think that no woman's lips had ever been as red as that bike. No low-slung foreign sports car with wire wheels and purring engine would ever look as powerful or as capable as that bike. No chrome would ever gleam with such purity, like the silver moon on a summers night. I had a big round headlight and a horn with a rubber bulb, and its frame looked as strong and solid as the biceps of Hercules. But it looked fast, too; it's handlebars sloped forward like an invitation to taste the wind, it's black rubber pedals unscarred by any foot before mine. Dad ran his fingers along the headlight, and then picked the bike up with one hand.<br />"Boy, it hardly weighs anything!" he marvelled."Lightest metal I've ever felt!" He put it down again, and it settled on its kickstand like an obedient but barely tamed animal."<br />(Boys toys)<br /><br />"I looked out, across my hometown. I looked at the green hills and the blue sky, and the distant roofs of Burton. Beside me, Rebel whimpered in a dogs dreams.<br /> I never knew what hate really was until I thought of somebody wrapping up a bomb and putting it in a church on a Sunday morning to kill little girls."<br /><br /><br />"This was early summer in Zephyr: an awakening to hazy morning heat, the sun gradually burning the haze off and the air getting so humid your shirt stuck to your skin by the time you'd walked to the mailbox and back. At noon the world seemed to pause on its axis, and not a bird dared to wing through the steaming blue. As afternoon rambled on, a few clouds rimmed with rule might build up from the northwest. You could sit on the porch, a glass of lemonade at your side and the radio tuned to a baseball game, and watch the clouds slowly roll toward you. After a while you might hear a distant thunder, and a zigzag of lighting would make the radio crackle. It might shower for thirty minutes or so, but most times the clouds just marched past with a rumble and grunt and not a drop of rain. As evening cooled the earth, the cicadas droned in their hundreds from the woods and lighting bugs rose from the grass. They got up in the trees and blinked, and they lit up the branches like Christmas decorations here on the edge of July. The stars came out, and some phase of the moon. If I played my cards right, I could talk my folks into letting me stay up late, like until eleven or so, and I would sit in front yard watching the lights of Zephyr go out. When enough lights were extinguished, the stars became much brighter. You could look up into the heart of the universe, and see the swirls of glowing stars. A soft breeze blew, bringing with it the sweet perfume of earth, and the trees rustled quietly in its passage. It was very hard, at times like this, not to think that the world was as well-ordered and precise as the Cartwright ranch on "Bonanza," or that in every house lived a "My Three Sons" family. I wished it were so, but I had seen pictures of a spreading dark, a burning man, and a bomb-wrecked church, and I was beginning to know the truth."<br />(Wish i/you was here?)<br /><br />"I had seen her naked. In all my life I had seen no female naked but my mother. I had been in the presence of Chile Willow only a short time, but what is time when a heart speaks? My heart was speaking to Chile Willow in that moment, as she bathed my cuts and gave me a smile. My heart was saying<i> if you were my girlfriend I would give you a hundred lighting bugs in a green glass jar, so you could always see your way. I would give you a meadow full of wildflowers, where no two blooms would ever be alike. I would give you mu bicycle, with it's golden eye to protect you. I would write a story for you, and make you a princes who lived in a white marble castle. If you would only like me, I would give you magic. If you would only like me.<br /> If you would only-"</i><br />(Love)<br />"This was to be my first experiment with it, and like any first experience, the feeling stays with you forever. What this was exactly I can't say, but it drove into my soul and made a home there. Everyone was watching me; everyone was listening to me. The words coming out of my mouth-the words I'd conceived and give birth to- were making time null and void; they were bringing together a roomful of people into a journey of common sights, sounds, and thoughts; they were leaving me and travelling into the minds and memories of people who had never been at Saxons Lake that chill, early morning in March. I could tell when I looked at them that those people were following me. And the greatest thing- the very greatest thing-is that they wanted to go where I led them."<br />(The joy of writing)<br /><br />"I sat beside him as the chill wind moved around us. Rebel made little whining noises deep in his throat. He let me pat him, but he was somewhere else. I remembered him as a puppy, full of boundless energy, enthralled by a yellow ball with a little bell in it. I remember the times we had raced each other, and like a true Southern gentleman he had always let me win. I remembered when he flew, over the hills of summer. Even if that had only been in my imagination, it was truer than true. I cried some.<br />More than some."<br /><br /></b>
</blockquote><br />Visit my webpage to read the interview during March 2012 &gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;<a href="http://more2read.com/review/interview-with-robert-r-mccammon/" rel="nofollow noopener">http://more2read.com/review/interview-with-robert-r-mccammon/</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="4692710637267333285" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2871384373" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2871384373" />
    <a title="Bradley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4213258-bradley"><img alt="Bradley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1508811508p2/4213258.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2871384373?book_show_action=true">Jun 26, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bradley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bradley" href="/user/show/4213258-bradley">Bradley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/36505403-boy-s-life">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=2019-shelf">2019-shelf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=traditional-fiction">traditional-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=fanboy-goes-squee">fanboy-goes-squee</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2871384373" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6943653370988393847">Do you know the feeling of eating some fresh-fresh-from-the-oven cornbread drizzled with some honey butter?<br/><br/>That's this entire novel. <br/><br/>A 12-year-old boy getting out of school, enjoying summer, then going back to school, in 60's Alabama. Sounds simple, right? But this is charming in not just a nostalgic kind of way a-la Stephen King's IT, but full of love, consideration, adventure, magical realism, murder, mystery, courage, and some of the best Coming-Of-Age writing I've ever come across.<br/><br/>It's more </span>
  <span id="freeText6943653370988393847" style="display:none">Do you know the feeling of eating some fresh-fresh-from-the-oven cornbread drizzled with some honey butter?<br /><br />That's this entire novel. <br /><br />A 12-year-old boy getting out of school, enjoying summer, then going back to school, in 60's Alabama. Sounds simple, right? But this is charming in not just a nostalgic kind of way a-la Stephen King's IT, but full of love, consideration, adventure, magical realism, murder, mystery, courage, and some of the best Coming-Of-Age writing I've ever come across.<br /><br />It's more than a horror or a YA or an in-depth real piece of homegrown Southern American Literature.<br />It's genuine. It deals honestly about racism and jerks and the Normal Rockwell way of life in a way that never comes off preachy or overwritten. But it deals with all of this and much more, including large swamp creatures and mythical stags in the forest, bootleggers and organized crime, and even the KKK and the new neo-nazi movement. But at no point did this diverge very far from the Boy's Life. :)<br /><br />Trust me. If you love writing like fresh cornbread, this novel will be like coming home.<br /><br />After all these years, I've just found a new favorite. I wasn't even close to being born when these events happened, but damn, I feel like I was THERE. :) Easily one of the very best novels of its kind.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6943653370988393847" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_612043365" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/612043365" />
    <a title="Carol" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7668522-carol"><img alt="Carol" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1546364878p2/7668522.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/612043365?book_show_action=true">May 10, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carol" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carol" href="/user/show/7668522-carol">Carol</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781416577782" href="/book/show/6278121-boy-s-life">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7668522-carol?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7668522-carol?shelf=1960-s">1960-s</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7668522-carol?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7668522-carol?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer612043365" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer375689429805607656"><b>"You Don't Have To Leave What Is, To Visit What Was"</b><p>Revisit the past by taking this sentimental journey into the 1960's in Zephyr, Alabama. Eleven year old Corey Mackenson and a memorable cast of well-defined characters <i>(OMG Vernon)</i> will make you both laugh and cry <i>many</i> times throughout the book. From a shocking murder comes haunting dreams, and from boyhood friendships comes both happiness and sorrow. There are creatures and ghosts, floods and bullies, and you'll <i>not</i> forget the wasp's from hell</p></span>
  <span id="freeText375689429805607656" style="display:none"><b>"You Don't Have To Leave What Is, To Visit What Was"</b><p>Revisit the past by taking this sentimental journey into the 1960's in Zephyr, Alabama. Eleven year old Corey Mackenson and a memorable cast of well-defined characters <i>(OMG Vernon)</i> will make you both laugh and cry <i>many</i> times throughout the book. From a shocking murder comes haunting dreams, and from boyhood friendships comes both happiness and sorrow. There are creatures and ghosts, floods and bullies, and you'll <i>not</i> forget the wasp's from hell or the magical "Lady" who can <i>see</i> that brings healing and wonder.</p><p>This award winning novel of growing up in a small southern town is just plain entertainment at its best. Loved it! Highly recommend.</p></span>
  <a data-text-id="375689429805607656" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1756367751" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1756367751" />
    <a title="Sue" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3642045-sue"><img alt="Sue" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1274829293p2/3642045.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1756367751?book_show_action=true">Sep 17, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sue" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sue" href="/user/show/3642045-sue">Sue</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780671742263" href="/book/show/970547.Boy_s_Life">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3642045-sue?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3642045-sue?shelf=library-book">library-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3642045-sue?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3642045-sue?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3642045-sue?shelf=read-2016">read-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3642045-sue?shelf=american-southern">american-southern</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1756367751" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5897706161186080208">Great, enjoyable book that hits on so many different emotional levels, and does it so well. I also very much appreciate the author's acknowledgement section at the end as the various cultural references take me back to moments from my youth and their attendant memories. And all just a week before my high school reunion! What a perfect moment to read such a memory-laden book.<br/><br/>As for the work itself, there is just so much here and I had so many different responses to it, all deftly drawn by McCammo</span>
  <span id="freeText5897706161186080208" style="display:none">Great, enjoyable book that hits on so many different emotional levels, and does it so well. I also very much appreciate the author's acknowledgement section at the end as the various cultural references take me back to moments from my youth and their attendant memories. And all just a week before my high school reunion! What a perfect moment to read such a memory-laden book.<br /><br />As for the work itself, there is just so much here and I had so many different responses to it, all deftly drawn by McCammon's prose. Laughter to shivers to near tears. I truly loved Cory's family and his observations of his parents. The pictures of Zephyr are of Anytown, USA in 1964 but for the fact of being in the South and some of what that brings to the table and, of course, that sprinkling of "the other" that rides through the story along with Cory on his bike. There seem to be magical influences if not magic itself. And there is evil, if not the devil. <br /><br />There is also some really wonderful writing. One of my favorite sections describes the local movie theater, the Lyric. Cody just had to look up that word in his dictionary:<br /><br /> <i>"Lyric," it said: "Melodic. Suitable for singing. A lyric poem.<br /> Of the lyre." That didn't seem to make much sense in regards<br /> to a movie theater, until I continued following lyre in my<br /> dictionary. Lyre took me into the story-poems sung by traveling<br /> minstrels back when there castles and kings. Which took me back <br /> to that wonderful word: story. It seemed to me at an early age<br /> that all human communication--whether it's TV, movies, or<br /> books--begins with somebody wanting to tell a story. That need<br /> to tell, to plug into a universal socket, is probably one of our <br /> grandest desires. And the need to hear stories, to live lives<br /> other than our own for even the briefest moment, is the key<br /> to the magic that was born in our bones.</i> (p 27)<br /><br />For, above all Boy's Life is a book of stories by a fictional boy who wants to be a storyteller. And the author is very likely in good part, Cory. <br /><br /><br />And, I dare say, most, if not all of us want to hear these stories, join in them, become a part of them for a while.<br /><br />Now I haven't spoken to the plot of this book...that is summarized well on Goodreads book page. It is the story of an eleven year old boy confronting life in 1964 Zephyr, Alabama. Where life had previously been pretty much an idyll, one day he learns there is evil and then he learns there are different degrees of evil in his and our world. McCammon uses the culture of the 1960s so well in advancing the story (ah that magical word!)...and as a person who was a teenager in 1964, I recognized and responded to those mentions strongly.<br /><br />I also strongly recommend this book to all who enjoy well written stories. This is the real deal! </span>
  <a data-text-id="5897706161186080208" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_74780699" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/74780699" />
    <a title="Mike (the Paladin)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2187043-mike-the-paladin"><img alt="Mike (the Paladin)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528431476p2/2187043.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/74780699?book_show_action=true">Oct 16, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mike (the Paladin)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mike (the Paladin)" href="/user/show/2187043-mike-the-paladin">Mike (the Paladin)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780671742263" href="/book/show/970547.Boy_s_Life">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2187043-mike-the-paladin?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2187043-mike-the-paladin?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2187043-mike-the-paladin?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2187043-mike-the-paladin?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer74780699" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2985591395968282257">This is a surprising book. My brother and I (who mostly agree on absolutely nothing) both enjoyed this book. We came to the conclusion it might be a generational thing. I'm a "Boomer" while he would be on the tail end of that designation if not just after it. A boy and his bicycle...a bike meant freedom then. I grew up in the foothills of the Smokies (Smoky Mountains)till I was 13. I was all over two counties on that bike. Then we moved to Dayton Ohio. There I covered the entire area on my Bike,</span>
  <span id="freeText2985591395968282257" style="display:none">This is a surprising book. My brother and I (who mostly agree on absolutely nothing) both enjoyed this book. We came to the conclusion it might be a generational thing. I'm a "Boomer" while he would be on the tail end of that designation if not just after it. A boy and his bicycle...a bike meant freedom then. I grew up in the foothills of the Smokies (Smoky Mountains)till I was 13. I was all over two counties on that bike. Then we moved to Dayton Ohio. There I covered the entire area on my Bike, Back then you could (and I did) park your bike at a bus stop (no lock) ride down town (to hit the available book outlets) ride the bus back. Your bike would still be there and you'd ride it home.<br /><br />The "paranormality" underlying this little town, the poison of racism, the relationship of Cory with his dad...as well as with his dog and his bike are all part of this book's magic. Happy, sad, cheerful, and melancholy, it's all here. This is one of my all time favorites. <br /><br />MaCammon in my opinion runs hot and cold. He's written books I liked and books I disliked and books that fall anywhere in between, but this book I loved. It has unsuspected depths and I believe will stay with you. </span>
  <a data-text-id="2985591395968282257" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('0iAL3M0KnyUJve5+Obxb49e9kcCaOR+uY5vJMb6PavZCMbexJB//ETYscMoey0AILegu0OdpEcEtMchnChcjaA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('q2L1pChq7sIRO+a9O/6tmWHafAuohRovOKBp+xodatY7c0nJwX+O9i6qeAkcibZym4/DG9XVFEB2CmitroUjSA==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer665401055147834721"><i>Robert Rick McCammon</i> was a full-time horror writer for many years. Among his many popular novels were the classics <i>Boy's Life</i> and <i>Swan Song</i>. After taking a hiatus for his family, he returned to writing with an interest in historical fiction.<br/><br/>The sixth book in his Matthew Corbett historical fiction series, <i>Freedom of the Mask</i>, was published in May 2016.<br/><br/>His next novel, a standalone book called <i>The Li</i></span>
  <span id="freeText665401055147834721" style="display:none"><i>Robert Rick McCammon</i> was a full-time horror writer for many years. Among his many popular novels were the classics <i>Boy's Life</i> and <i>Swan Song</i>. After taking a hiatus for his family, he returned to writing with an interest in historical fiction.<br /><br />The sixth book in his Matthew Corbett historical fiction series, <i>Freedom of the Mask</i>, was published in May 2016.<br /><br />His next novel, a standalone book called <i>The Listener</i>, was published in February 2018 by Cemetery Dance.<br /><br />His newest novel, <i>Cardinal Black</i>, is the seventh book in the Matthew Corbett series. It is available now from Cemetery Dance.<br /><br />McCammon resides in Birmingham, Alabama. He is currently working on the eighth Matthew Corbett novel, <i>The King of Shadows</i>.</span>

      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/16685995-boy-s-life">Quotes from Boy&#39;s Life</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;You know, I do believe in magic. I was born and raised in a magic time, in a magic town, among magicians. Oh, most everybody else didn’t realize we lived in that web of magic, connected by silver filaments of chance and circumstance. But I knew it all along. When I was twelve years old, the world was my magic lantern, and by its green spirit glow I saw the past, the present and into the future. You probably did too; you just don’t recall it. See, this is my opinion: we all start out knowing magic. We are born with whirlwinds, forest fires, and comets inside us. We are born able to sing to birds and read the clouds and see our destiny in grains of sand. But then we get the magic educated right out of our souls. We get it churched out, spanked out, washed out, and combed out. We get put on the straight and narrow and told to be responsible. Told to act our age. Told to grow up, for God’s sake. And you know why we were told that? Because the people doing the telling were afraid of our wildness and youth, and because the magic we knew made them ashamed and sad of what they’d allowed to wither in themselves.<br /><br />After you go so far away from it, though, you can’t really get it back. You can have seconds of it. Just seconds of knowing and remembering. When people get weepy at movies, it’s because in that dark theater the golden pool of magic is touched, just briefly. Then they come out into the hard sun of logic and reason again and it dries up, and they’re left feeling a little heartsad and not knowing why. When a song stirs a memory, when motes of dust turning in a shaft of light takes your attention from the world, when you listen to a train passing on a track at night in the distance and wonder where it might be going, you step beyond who you are and where you are. For the briefest of instants, you have stepped into the magic realm.<br /><br />That’s what I believe.<br /><br />The truth of life is that every year we get farther away from the essence that is born within us. We get shouldered with burdens, some of them good, some of them not so good. Things happen to us. Loved ones die. People get in wrecks and get crippled. People lose their way, for one reason or another. It’s not hard to do, in this world of crazy mazes. Life itself does its best to take that memory of magic away from us. You don’t know it’s happening until one day you feel you’ve lost something but you’re not sure what it is. It’s like smiling at a pretty girl and she calls you “sir.” It just happens.<br /><br />These memories of who I was and where I lived are important to me. They make up a large part of who I’m going to be when my journey winds down. I need the memory of magic if I am ever going to conjure magic again. I need to know and remember, and I want to tell you.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/214560-you-know-i-do-believe-in-magic-i-was-born">588 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;After years of having a dog, you know him. You know the meaning of his snuffs and grunts and barks. Every twitch of the ears is a question or statement, every wag of the tail is an exclamation.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/500-after-years-of-having-a-dog-you-know-him-you">266 likes</a>
